# products_reviewsFlat

The `products_reviewsFlat` view should be used when you want to look at individual reviews for each product in your data set in a CSV format.  It will split each review for a product into its own row.  All other fields will repeat in each row.

[block:api-header]
{
  "type": "basic",
  "title": "Included Fields"
}
[/block]

[block:parameters]
{
  "data": {
    "h-0": "Field",
    "0-0": "`asins`",
    "1-0": "`brand`",
    "2-0": "`categories`",
    "3-0": "`colors`",
    "4-0": "`count`",
    "5-0": "`dateAdded`",
    "6-0": "`dateUpdated`",
    "7-0": "`descriptions`",
    "8-0": "`dimension`",
    "9-0": "`ean`",
    "10-0": "`features`",
    "11-0": "`flavors`",
    "12-0": "`imageURLs`",
    "13-0": "`isbn`",
    "14-0": "`keys`",
    "15-0": "`manufacturer`",
    "16-0": "`manufacturerNumber`",
    "17-0": "`merchants`",
    "18-0": "`name`",
    "19-0": "`prices`",
    "20-0": "`reviews`",
    "21-0": "`sizes`",
    "22-0": "`skus`",
    "23-0": "`sourceURLs`",
    "24-0": "`upc`",
    "25-0": "`vin`",
    "26-0": "`websiteID`",
    "27-0": "`weight`",
    "h-1": "Included Sub-fields",
    "7-1": "`dateSeen`\n`sourceURLs`\n`value`",
    "10-1": "`key`\n`value`",
    "17-1": "`address`\n`availability`\n`city`\n`country`\n`dateSeen`\n`name`\n`phone`\n`postalCode`\n`province`",
    "19-1": "`amountMin`\n`amountMax`\n`availability`\n`color`\n`condition`\n`count`\n`currency`\n`dateAdded`\n`dateSeen`\n`flavor`\n`isSale`\n`merchant`\n`offer`\n`returnPolicy`\n`shipping`\n`size`\n`source`\n`sourceURLs`\n`warranty`",
    "20-1": "`date`\n`dateAdded`\n`dateSeen`\n`didPurchase`\n`doRecommend`\n`numHelpful`\n`rating`\n`sourceURLs`\n`text`\n`title`\n`userCity`\n`username`\n`userProvince`",
    "22-1": "`sourceURLs`\n`value`",
    "0-1": "N/A",
    "1-1": "N/A",
    "2-1": "N/A",
    "3-1": "N/A",

  },
  "cols": 2,

}
[/block]

bought these speakers when I got my '93 Saturn SL2. After seventeen years, the original speakers were blown. I needed some good tunes for my daily 40-mile each-way commute. First, I replaced the stereo head unit with a Pioneer DEH-11E, a 200W-peak unit (the stock FM radio with blown speakers sounded awful). Then I replaced the speakers with these. They sound great, and they carry bass, mids, and treble tones very well. However, while they claim to handle up to 75W each (300W with all four speakers), they distort slightly under the stress of volume levels above 90 on the 200W (50W each speaker) Pioneer.Still, this is nothing to complain about if they're only being used for replacing bad OEM speakers. They work nicely with my mid-level stereo, and I am fully confident that if they were hooked to a stock unit, they would more than carry their weight. In my case, Saturns have relatively high levels of road noise and rattling I'm able to compensate for most of the road noise by cranking up the mids on the equalizer. And in the small cabin of a compact car, I can't really turn it up to full power without getting a headache...They fit nicely into the 6.75' stock speaker spaces of my Saturn, no modifications were required. One final note: if you're planning on using the included grilles, be careful when installing them. They attach to the speakers directly at the outside edge of the paper, tearing it easily. Not to mention the grilles are painted rather thinly, so they scratch easily. I managed to not damage the speakers, but I opted to reuse the stock grilles instead... Think of it this way: you're less likely to get broken into if everyone thinks you're using stock!For their very low price (37 shipped for four speakers), and great performance, I highly recommend these speakers.\",\"Great OEM Speaker this same model in black to install in a 2013 Sienna. First impression, this unit is huge! It is pretty heavy, so be prepared to reinforce your mounting point. No way would I trust the headliner to support this unit. After the install, I must say I was very impressed with the picture quality. The monitor is big, and the viewing angles are great.One glaring issue I noticed right away, the output volume for the FM modulator is set from the factory at 50, and you cannot change it. This means that in order to listen to a DVD over your vehicle's FM radio, you must turn the radio volume WAY up. This causes noticeable static in the sound. And if you forget to turn the volume back down before turning off the vehicle, you will be greeted with a deafening static roar as the DVD player powers off before the stereo.I have to admit, if the volume was the only issue, I could still recommend this model, however, after only 2 months of use, it has stopped playing DVD's. The unit will power on normally, and all menus function, but as soon as a DVD is loaded, the picture appears extremely pixelated and choppy, eventually freezing all together. This has happened on multiple discs, and yes I have made sure none are scratched or dirty. This is further complicated by the pretty much useless SD card functionality that will not save the video position when the vehicle is powered off. It won't even save the SD setting, making you navigate several menus to select SD playback at all. Video playback on SD was pretty choppy as well, even on lower bitrates.I am currently in the process of RMA'ing the unit to Tview, as I am outside of the Amazon return window. The only way to get the video to come back on the main screen was to change the input mode, from DVD to aux input (Backup Camera) and back to DVD again, or turn the whole unit off/on again. Once the main screen has video again, it would stay on anywhere from a few seconds to many hours. It was very aggravating - intermittent. Shipping.\"\",\"\"sourceURLs\"\":[\"\"http://www.amazon.com/Tview-T20DVFD-GR-20-Inch-Built--Player/dp/B009EQEBQA\"\"]}]\",,\"2013-01-28T00:00:00Z\",\"2015-12-03T01:27:33Z\",\"2015-12-03T00:00:00Z\",,,,,,\"http://www.amazon.com/Tview-T20DVFD-GR-20-Inch-Built--Player/dp/B009EQEBQA\",\"Purchased this same model in black to install in a 2013 Sienna. First impression, this unit is huge! It is pretty heavy, so be prepared to reinforce your mounting point. No way would I trust the headliner to support this unit. After the install, I must say I was very impressed with the picture quality. The monitor is big, and the viewing angles are great.One glaring issue I noticed right away, the output volume for the FM modulator is set from the factory at 50, and you cannot change it. This means that in order to listen to a DVD over your vehicle's FM radio, you must turn the radio volume WAY up. This causes noticeable static in the sound. And if you forget to turn the volume back down before turning off the vehicle, you will be greeted with a deafening static roar as the DVD player powers off before the stereo.I have to admit, if the volume was the only issue, I could still recommend this model, however, after only 2 months of use, it has stopped playing DVD's. The unit will power on normally, and all menus function, but as soon as a DVD is loaded, the picture appears extremely pixelated and choppy, eventually freezing all together. This has happened on multiple discs, and yes I have made sure none are scratched or dirty. This is further complicated by the pretty much useless SD card functionality that will not save the video position when the vehicle is powered off. It won't even save the SD setting, making you navigate several menus to select SD playback at all. Video playback on SD was pretty choppy as well, even on lower bitrates.I am currently in the process of RMA'ing the unit to Tview, as I am outside of the Amazon return window. Beyond that I'm not impressed. We received the first one with NO packing inside the box, no wires and no remote. The monitor was just bouncing around inside the box. We returned it and received a second one next day. After installation we noticed a few small white specks in the screen, like where the light behind is shining through. The remote works about half the time, and some of the commands on it are misspelled (ie: return is spelled RETURE). As other reviewers have said, the sound is locked at 50, grayed out where you can't adjust it. Several of the other options on the remote seem to have no purpose...they do nothing when the button is touched. The USB works fine, but it does not play back from the last point when you have to leave the vehicle. Upon returning to your trip you have to start over and fast forward to the point you left off. Wireless headsets don't work well with this, either. I tried several different brands of headsets and received a lot of static in the sound. I've tested them with other players and they work fine, so it's just this particular player. I have to keep an aux cable run from the back of the player to my van stereo, and have to remember to turn down the sound when finished watching, otherwise it nearly blows my speakers when radio or cd is wanted again. The menus are so much easier to understand than other TVs I've wrangled with. External media via USB works well. I bought a Samsung DVD player too and they pair with the same remote which is a nice bonus. All that is great. I have two major complaints.1- Sound. I have a set of computer speakers that I plugged into the mini jack audio out of the TV. You cannot control the external speakers with the TV remote by this method. Since my computer speakers do not have a remote it means I have to get up and walk across the room to turn the volume down or just use the TV speakers which are pretty worthless due to the nature of every flat screen TV - they must have the speakers in the back by design. I contacted Samsung support and they confirmed that the mini jack audio out is a fixed volume and cannot be altered with the remote.2- Wifi. Maybe I have a dud, but as a wireless device this TV is pointless. I don't have cable TV. I don't watch broadcast TV. I use Netflix, Hulu and Amazon almost exclusively for video entertainment. This means a solid connection to the internet is a must. The TV has major issues with my wifi. I have troubleshooted this issue in every way I know how: network settings, rebooting cable modem and router several times, starting the devices in order from modem to wifi router to TV. Scroll to bottom of review to read 2014 updates -- I am returning this TV.This TV was released in February as Samsung's budget 32-inch As of this writing it's going for around 475, so about 200 more than the budget Smart TV's from Vizio. First my review of the TV, then I'll compare it to Vizio's product VIZIO E320i-A0 32-inch 720p 60Hz LED Smart HDTV, which I have also purchased and decided to return in favor of this unit. As you would expect, the TV has a great picture. Smooth, no pixelation, even sports look great on here. It's advertised as a 60hz -- but then the box refers to 120 Tru Motion so I'm not sure what to make of that, but suffice it to say that refresh rates are good. The remote control is decent - lights up at night and has good sized buttons, but I'd like dedicated buttons for Netflix and Amazon VOD. This TV begins to blur the line between TV and computer... the internet browser is competent, but pretty frustrating to use without a keyboard. You can hook up a USB keyboard through the TV's slot. This TV does NOT accommodate bluetooth keyboards, so wireless is out of the picture. I believe the next model up of Samsung (the 6000 series) accommodates Bluetooth as that is referenced in the manual. The Smart Apps section reveals many apps (Pandora, Picasa, etc) that you would find on your Smartphone. Due to the dual core of the TV's processor, apps load quickly and the TV starts immediately. As for the sound, it's really decent to good. You're not ever going to get good base etc without an external sound source on any HDTV... but this provides a good viewing experience.Read more\",\"Excellent picture AND sound, software needs some
